# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Informer Cache Event Handler Chain

## Your Task

Trace the event handler chain from API server watch events to informer cache updates in kubernetes/kubernetes. Find the Go source files implementing the ListWatch, the DeltaFIFO queue, and the cache.Store handler dispatch that notifies registered event handlers.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

79-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced the event handler chain from API server watch events to informer cache updates. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Event Handler Chain Summary

The flow consists of 10 key stages:

1. **API Server Watch** - Kubernetes API server streams watch events
2. **ListWatch Interface** - Provides List() and Watch() methods to the Reflector
3. **Reflector** - Watches API via ListWatch and feeds events to the DeltaFIFO queue
4. **DeltaFIFO Queue** - Accumulates events as ordered Delta objects
5. **Controller** - Orchestrates Reflector and pops items from queue
6. **SharedIndexInformer** - Receives Deltas and processes them via HandleDeltas()
7. **Delta Processing** - Updates cache and invokes handler callbacks
8. **SharedProcessor** - Distributes notifications to all registered listeners
9. **ProcessorListener** - Buffers and dispatches events to individual handlers
10. **Event Handler** - User-registered handler receives OnAdd/OnUpdate/OnDelete callbacks

## Key Files Identified

The core implementation spans these files in both kubernetes/kubernetes and client-go:
- **tools/cache/listwatch.go** - ListerWatcher interface and ListWatch implementation
- **tools/cache/delta_fifo.go** - DeltaFIFO queue implementation
- **tools/cache/reflector.go** - Reflector that watches API and feeds events
- **tools/cache/controller.go** - Controller managing Reflector and processDeltas function
- **tools/cache/shared_informer.go** - SharedIndexInformer, SharedProcessor, and ProcessorListener

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbols, and a detailed narrative explanation of the event flow.

buffer\\n   - Sends buffered notifications to nextCh\\n   - run() reads from nextCh and invokes the appropriate handler method synchronously\\n   - Catches panics during handler invocation and continues processing\\n\\n10. **Event Handler Invocation**:\\n    - Handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList) for added objects\\n    - Handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj) for modified objects  \\n    - Handler.OnDelete(obj) for deleted objects\\n    - Handlers are called synchronously within the processorListener.run() goroutine\\n\\nThis architecture ensures that:\\n- Events from the API server flow through a FIFO queue\\n- The cache is updated atomically before handlers are notified\\n- Multiple handlers can be registered and each receives a copy of events\\n- Handlers can specify custom resync periods\\n- Event ordering is preserved per object\\n- The system gracefully handles handler panics\"\n}\n",
